}

The reasoning behind this decision is that by setting X to 0.5, we create a significant enough penalty to discourage players from overconsuming apples in low-density regions. If a player chooses to overconsume, they would lose half an apple, which is a significant portion of their potential gain. This apple would then be equally distributed to the other players, promoting fairness and cooperation. 

By proposing this contract, we can encourage sustainable harvesting practices and ensure that the apple supply is maintained for future rounds. This strategy balances the need for immediate gain with the need for long-term sustainability, and could potentially yield higher rewards in the long run.

The reasoning behind this decision is that by setting X to 0.5, we are creating a significant enough penalty to discourage players from over-harvesting in low-density regions. This will help to maintain a healthy apple population, which is beneficial for all players in the long run. If X was set too low, the penalty might not be significant enough to deter over-harvesting. If X was set too high, it could discourage players from harvesting apples altogether, which is not the goal. The goal is to encourage sustainable harvesting practices. Therefore, X=0.5 seems to be a reasonable choice.
